Clio2 calibration data for 2014A run (March-April 2014).

Navigation Within This Page:
GoTo Raw Flats
GoTo Raw Darks


Raw Flats

 Listing after the zip file is a screen print out by readclio.pro.
Bias is ~5000 counts so look for counts well above that to have enough signal to build a flat. If you are doing "lights on" minus "lights off" (i.e. "twi-bright" minus "twi-dark"), use frames near the bias in counts for the dark/"lights off"/"twi-dark".
Data require a linearity calibration above 27,000 counts so best not to use those frames for the flat, either.

Raw Darks

*NOTE: Header keywords "TEMP1" and "TEMP2" record the temperature in Kelvin of the detector (TEMP1, set to 55K) and the optics (TEMP2, set to 77K). If you note that the Darks seem noisy or the counts are climbing, check TEMP1 and TEMP2, and if they are a few degrees too high, you might not want to use those darks. So you can check the FITS header to make sure your darks are about at the right temperature as compared to your images.

;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;







309.5MB
*Note the steeply rising counts at the very end in the very long exposure Darks. The Clio2 detector is kept at 55K via a solid nitrogen pump, but the dewar is filled every morning with 77K liquid nitrogen - thus, filling the dewar briefly warms up the detector for a few hours, and then it cools again. We do the darks at the end of the night (usually starting around 7:30am), and my guess is that this set of darks is so long that it hadn't finished by the time the dewar was filled (usually around 9am). Thus, the darks with steeply rising counts should be viewed as bad data and should not be used.
